    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_3312321126" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3312321126" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3312321126?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780151685509" href="/book/show/1184633.The_Old_Man_Who_Read_Love_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=south-american">south-american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=book-to-film">book-to-film</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3312321126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3121744579618938947"><b>”On March 1, 2020, after returning from a conference in Portugal, Luis Sepúlveda was confirmed as the first man in the Asturias region of Spain to be infected by COVID-19. By March 11, it was reported that Sepúlveda was in critical condition, that he was in an induced coma with assisted breathing due to multiple organ failure in an Oviedo hospital.He died on April 16 due to the virus.”--Wikipedia</b><br/><br/>This novel won the Tigre Juan Award in 1988. It was his first novel. <br/><br/><b>”He could read!<br/><br/>It was the most i</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3121744579618938947" style="display:none"><b>”On March 1, 2020, after returning from a conference in Portugal, Luis Sepúlveda was confirmed as the first man in the Asturias region of Spain to be infected by COVID-19. By March 11, it was reported that Sepúlveda was in critical condition, that he was in an induced coma with assisted breathing due to multiple organ failure in an Oviedo hospital.He died on April 16 due to the virus.”--Wikipedia</b><br /><br />This novel won the Tigre Juan Award in 1988. It was his first novel. <br /><br /><b>”He could read!<br /><br />It was the most important discovery of his whole life. He could read. He possessed the antidote to the deadly poison of old age. He could read. But he had nothing to read.”</b><br /><br />Antonio Jose Bolivar Proano has lived in the jungle of Ecuador for nearly forty years. He once lived with the Shuar natives, but tragic circumstances required him to leave his adopted tribe and settle with his fellow whites in the small village of El Idilio. He was once a great hunter, but now he has become old and enjoys nothing more than losing himself in the pain and anguish of doomed love stories. A dentist who shows up twice a year to extract teeth from the villagers brings him two new books. The dentist knows a hooker who has the exact same taste in books as Bolivar.<br /><br />Bolivar would be quite content to lead his simple life and while away the hours of his days enthralled by the passions of fictional people, but a man is killed by a female ocelot after he killed her cubs and wounded her mate. Bolivar is forced to join the hunt for the female by the fat, wife-beating mayor, whom everyone calls the Slimy Toad behind his back. <i>”His wife will kill him. She’s piling up hatred but hasn’t got enough yet. These things take time.”</i> <br /><br />These things take time. I wonder how many wives right now are contemplating creative ways to murder their husbands after being quarantined with them for several weeks. :-) Let’s hope these are only fantasies and that the piling up of unhappiness merely leads to divorce, not murder most foul. <br /><br />Bolivar finds what is left of a settler and a dead American, killed by the grief-stricken ocelot. The jungle is rather tidy with debris. <i>”The American was lying a few yards further on. The ants had done a magnificent job, leaving their bones as smooth as plaster. The American’s skeleton was receiving the last attention of the ants. They were carrying away his straw-colored hair strand by strand, like tiny women woodcutters felling coppery trees, to strengthen the entrance tunnel to their anthill.”</i><br /><br />The ocelot has a taste for blood now, the blood of man, and she won’t stop killing them until her last breath. <br /><br />Bolivar doesn’t want to be the one, but he knows he has to be the one. He soon finds himself in a desperate struggle to kill an animal he sympathizes with before she manages to kill him. I keep thinking about <i>The Old Man and the Sea,</i> as one man battles the forces of nature. This is considered an ecological novel and certainly shines a light on the negative impact of the West on those regions of the world that were existing in balanced harmony before the trudge of their big feet, the jangle of their equipment, their loud voices, their arrogance, their pathological need to hunt, and their fascination in gazing upon primitive cultures (reminding me of those who search out poverty porn) turn a jungle into chaos.<br /><br />I really love the sweet, subtle power of this novel. The resistance of a culture to technology and the metal monsters of guns and machines. The respect that the Shuar people show the jungle and the wonder they feel as they encounter mystical elements that seemingly defy science. I love thinking about this leather-skinned, old man pondering the mysteries of love as he listens to the river and turns the pages of a book. <br /><br />There is a movie based on the book, starring Richard Dreyfuss, that was released in 2001. I’ve not been able to track down a copy to watch, but certainly intend to when I finally find a way. <br /><br />Sepulveda’s life reads like a novel, not a love story, but one fraught with constant danger. He was arrested twice in his home country of Chile and tortured by the General Augusto Pinochet regime. He was an ardent supporter of the rights of people. He eventually was released after pressure by Amnesty International and chose to live in Germany because of his great love for the literature of that country. If you get a chance, do read about his life on Wikipedia. He was certainly a man who used the power of his pen to try and expose the abuses of those in power. It is unfortunate that it took a news story about his death appearing on my cell phone for me to be motivated to finally read one of his books. <br /><br />This is a slender, but powerful book. You won’t regret spending an afternoon with Bolivar and his struggle with his conscience as he tracks down a cat who has every right to be vengeful. <br /><br />If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br />I also have a Facebook blogger page at:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a> and an Instagram account <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/jeffreykeeten/">https://www.instagram.com/jeffreykeeten/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3121744579618938947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_584969806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/584969806" />
    <a title="Mike Puma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4193758-mike-puma"><img alt="Mike Puma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434667514p2/4193758.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/584969806?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike Puma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike Puma" href="/user/show/4193758-mike-puma">Mike Puma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780151685509" href="/book/show/1184633.The_Old_Man_Who_Read_Love_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4193758-mike-puma?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4193758-mike-puma?shelf=chilean-author">chilean-author</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer584969806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2172622987409305673"><p>Briefly: This compelling and efficient novella grabs readers and quickly embeds them within the life of an aging Ecuadoran whose first, and only love, has died after a brief and unproductive marriage, leaving the much younger Antonio José Bolívar Proaño procreatively unaccomplished, as well as, a failure as a settler in a new community. Unable to return to his previous village, “the poor forgive everything but failure,” Antonio settles in the village of El Idilio (the Idyll—get a sense of how th</p></span>
  <span id="freeText2172622987409305673" style="display:none"><p>Briefly: This compelling and efficient novella grabs readers and quickly embeds them within the life of an aging Ecuadoran whose first, and only love, has died after a brief and unproductive marriage, leaving the much younger Antonio José Bolívar Proaño procreatively unaccomplished, as well as, a failure as a settler in a new community. Unable to return to his previous village, “the poor forgive everything but failure,” Antonio settles in the village of El Idilio (the Idyll—get a sense of how this begins to work?) where his humble life includes joining the hunting expeditions of the Shuar, a people very in touch with the environment and tradition, but try as he does, he remains, ‘like them, but not one of them,’ as an inadvertent violation of tradition and friendship all too quickly reveals. Later in life, he is comforted by visits by a travelling dentist who brings novels—love stories—premised on the recommendations of the dentist’s favored prostitute. The idyllic life of Antonio is complicated by the constantly sweating village mayor (variously referred to as ‘the fat man’ or Slimey Toad) and an unforgiving ocelot. Honor, tradition, wisdom, all themes in a slight volume that readers will breeze through as danger mounts and admiration for the old man grows.</p><p>You can keep Hemingway’s old man, I’ll take Sepúlveda’s any day. 4-and-some-fraction stars, in this case rounded down, not because of a failure, rather because it could have been so, so much longer. Very nicely done.</p><p>Nearly forgot a quote:</p><blockquote>even as he was now preparing to do with the books the dentist had brought him, books that lay beckoning to him from the high table, innocent of the chaotic vista of a past that Antonio José Bolívar preferred to forget, leaving open the wells of memory, to be filled with the delights and torments of loves that outlasted time.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="2172622987409305673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3295284018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3295284018" />
    <a title="Glenn Russell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23385697-glenn-russell"><img alt="Glenn Russell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505195595p2/23385697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3295284018?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glenn Russell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glenn Russell" href="/user/show/23385697-glenn-russell">Glenn Russell</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23385697-glenn-russell?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3295284018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18094330571876105083"><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587569751i/29337953._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Luis Sepúlveda, (October 4, 1949 – April 16, 2020)<br/><br/>Luis Sepúlveda, a sensitive man, a beautiful man, a writer and journalist from Chile who died of COVID-19 this spring.<br/><br/><i>The Old Man Who Read Love Stories</i> is one of Luis Sepúlveda's most beloved books, a timeless classic that speaks powerfully to all of us in our worldwide community. <br/><br/>Similar to Hermann Hesse's <i>Sidhartha</i> and Ernest Hemingway's <i>The Old Man and the Sea</i>, Luis Sepúlveda's short tale possesses a deeply moving, universal, mythic quality th</span>
  <span id="freeText18094330571876105083" style="display:none"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587569751i/29337953._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Luis Sepúlveda, (October 4, 1949 – April 16, 2020)<br><br>Luis Sepúlveda, a sensitive man, a beautiful man, a writer and journalist from Chile who died of COVID-19 this spring.<br><br><i>The Old Man Who Read Love Stories</i> is one of Luis Sepúlveda's most beloved books, a timeless classic that speaks powerfully to all of us in our worldwide community. <br><br>Similar to Hermann Hesse's <i>Sidhartha</i> and Ernest Hemingway's <i>The Old Man and the Sea</i>, Luis Sepúlveda's short tale possesses a deeply moving, universal, mythic quality that will touch a reader's heart. I know, I know, sounds like cliché but in this case it's true.<br><br>Turning to the novella itself, we read how old Antonio José Bolívar Proaño would like nothing more than to be left alone in his hut, standing at his high table, reading his love stories. But, alas, life has a way of intruding. <br><br>One day when the old man is among the townspeople, Shuar Indians bring along a dead fair-haired gringo. The fat major immediately claims the Shuar killed him, sliced the white man's neck with a machete. But Antonio José Bolívar Proaño knows otherwise - he points out the telling details, the scent of piss, the claw marks of a female ocelot.<br><br>Ah, a killer on the loose! <br><br>Thus begins the tale. But not a word more about the unfolding journey into the jungle. Rather, I'll switch to one of the most charming parts of Luis Sepúlveda's delightful tale: <br><br>We read the way in which Antonio José Bolívar Proaño came to read love stories, pouring over books hour after hour, day after day, assisted by a magnifying glass. And then the old man hit on one novel where he found what he was really after, a love story containing love everywhere, where the characters "suffered and mingled love and pain so beautifully that his magnifying glass was awash with tears." Antonio José Bolívar Proaño read and reread the novel hundreds of times. <br><br>You may ask: What's the title of that very special novel? Answer: <i>The Rosary</i> by the British author Florence Louisa Barclay, 1862-1921. <i>The Rosary</i> is available via Project Gutenberg. Link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/3659/3659-h/3659-h.htm">http://www.gutenberg.org/files/3659/3...</a><br><br>I purposely kept my review brief. You will have to experience the magic of <i>The Old Man Who Read Love Stories</i> for yourself.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1588458791i/29400658._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="18094330571876105083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2259942931763754941">Oh, I must have erased my original review!!<br/>This book is one of my favorite books of all times. An absolute gem. It´s poignant, beautiful, simple and complex at the same time.   <span id="freeText2259942931763754941" style="display:none">Oh, I must have erased my original review!!<br />This book is one of my favorite books of all times. An absolute gem. It´s poignant, beautiful, simple and complex at the same time. You can read it as a simple story, or you can peel the layers, like an onion.<br />Themes of ecology, love, solitude, exile.....it´s all there, with a little adventure thrown in. The most unique of his works, in my opinion. His other novels are mostly thrillers, and entertaining. But this one has a special quality that touches me. I tell people, if you ¨get¨this book, you ¨get¨me. There was a movie made-good, because a lot of Sepúlveda´s works would lend themselves to screen adaptations easily. Don´t know that my image of José Antonio matches with Richard Dreyfuss, but would still love to see it. Alas, not formatted for the US....:(<br />I have never recommended this book to anyone who has said that they didn´t like it. I love it so much, I include it in one of my courses. And my students love it, even though most of them are younger than the novel.<br />Students of any age can read this story, though I´m not certain the message would reach middle-school children the way it might reach high-school students.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=cultural-shock">cultural-shock</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6753400-gabrielle?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1787879196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16495182811888077929">When you work as an executive assistant, 80% of what makes the job good and interesting is whether or not you get along with your boss. And I don’t want to brag, but my boss is ze best! When we started working together, he quickly noticed I always had books kicking around and spent most of my lunch breaks with my nose buried in the pages of my latest read. One day, he handed me some stuff to file, but also a skinny little book.<br/><br/>“It’s one of my favourites: I hope you’ll like it!”<br/><br/>Seriously. Best bo</span>
  <span id="freeText16495182811888077929" style="display:none">When you work as an executive assistant, 80% of what makes the job good and interesting is whether or not you get along with your boss. And I don’t want to brag, but my boss is ze best! When we started working together, he quickly noticed I always had books kicking around and spent most of my lunch breaks with my nose buried in the pages of my latest read. One day, he handed me some stuff to file, but also a skinny little book.<br /><br />“It’s one of my favourites: I hope you’ll like it!”<br /><br />Seriously. Best boss ever.<br /><br />“The old man who read love stories” is the story of a man named Antonio Jose Bolivar. He lives in a tiny village in Ecuador, and eventually leaves the comfort of his beloved books to hunt a man-killing panther in the Amazonian forest. Such a simple story at first glance – but don’t be fooled by the low page count. This novella is written with the musical elegance that I have come to associate with South American writers: each word is chosen carefully and flows right off the tongue if you should happen to be reading out loud.<br /><br />Not simply a love letter to books, and their immense power to make life better, it is also a sad, adoring homage to the great South American forests that are being inexorably destroyed. The life and rituals of aboriginal tribes living in the forest are detailed, as are the beautiful fauna and flora to be found there. Contrasted with the crassness and greed of elected officials, poachers, gold diggers and other unsavory characters who can’t respect and appreciate the world they are violating, the murderous ocelot becomes a symbol of a wild part of nature that fights back against the invader, trying to defend its environment against an enemy that can’t possibly be stopped.<br /><br />It reminded me in many ways of one of my favorite reads, “The man who planted trees” by Jean Giono; both stories are about lonely men who have a love of nature and solitude. But “The old man who read love stories” is much more brutal and raw than Giono’s lyrical tale. Where Elzear Bouffier reforests an entire region, Antonio Jose Bolivar cannot do anything but witness the destruction of the forest he lives in. <br /><br />A very good, quick read that I recommend to all fans of South American literature. Thank you Richard, for sharing your book with me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16495182811888077929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3412232385" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3412232385" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143117-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571421692p2/3143117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3412232385?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3143117-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788472236554" href="/book/show/882088.Un_viejo_que_le_a_novelas_de_amor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=espa%C3%B1ol">español</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=latin-american-lit">latin-american-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143117-david?shelf=chileno">chileno</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3412232385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14244493911300594459">I start with an apology. I had never heard of Luis Sepúlveda, a Chilean writer living in Spain until I read in El País that in died this year of coronavirus. He was 71. How truly sad for his family. How sad that I did not know of him.<br/><br/>The El País article noted this book was his most well known and after a little delay, as his books had sold out, I finally received a copy.<br/><br/>First, let us start with the beautiful and enchanting cover. Painted by Wolfgang Rieder it seduces one into wanting to read thi</span>
  <span id="freeText14244493911300594459" style="display:none">I start with an apology. I had never heard of Luis Sepúlveda, a Chilean writer living in Spain until I read in El País that in died this year of coronavirus. He was 71. How truly sad for his family. How sad that I did not know of him.<br /><br />The El País article noted this book was his most well known and after a little delay, as his books had sold out, I finally received a copy.<br /><br />First, let us start with the beautiful and enchanting cover. Painted by Wolfgang Rieder it seduces one into wanting to read this book.<br /><br />Second, the title, The old man who read romance novels, along with the cover image easily makes one think of Garcia Garcia Marquez. I am happy to report that other than being set in the Amazon rainforest, it bears little resemblance. There is no magical realism although their is a sense of “wonder” at nature itself. And nature is hardly magical in the rainforest. Case in point, when a colonist died, by the next day, the ants and other insects stripped the body down to its bones. Nope not magical.<br /><br />Now the only similarity I would strike is the “magical” names. The book is set in the idyllic place of El Idilio, which is hardly a magical place. The shabby huts lined with beer cases and mud is constantly rained upon. The old man is named Antonio José Bolivar Proaño and his wife is Dolores Encarnación del Santísimo Sacramento Estupiñán Otavalo. That should win an award for the most beautiful name ever. <br /><br />Third, is the size of the book. It is only 137 pages long so it falls in as a novela. A far cry from 100 Years of Solitude running in at over 600 pages.<br /><br />And yet, this was a very enjoyable read. Twice a year a dentist would come to see the people of the the Amazonian outpost. Enter the old man who makes a fool of the mayor when a body is brought in by natives. The mayor claims the natives robbed and killed the colonist. The old man points out a tigrillo or leopard killed him. After clearing up the murder, the old man gets what he came for - romance novels that the dentist brings him. <br /><br />We get the background on the old man, his love of romance novels, and his more acute ties to the shuar natives. Shades of the environmental and politics like Mario Vargas Llosa but this book stands on its own. And of course, after a visit from some gringos from North America, the mayor wants the tigrillo caught. A hunt is on. There is a lot thrown into a short book.<br /><br />For me there was something magical, enjoyable or just caught me at the right time. It is very sad that I had not known about this author before but it demands attention. Sadly for the wrong reasons.<br /><br />4.5 rating</span>
  <a data-text-id="14244493911300594459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5647943-ben-winch?shelf=chilean">chilean</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer777131538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8661736256472709781">Should be a bestseller. Could easily have been overpowered by sentimentality but it wasn’t. A kind of murder mystery where a big cat’s the killer and the mystery’s solved as soon as it’s introduced, but then they’ve gotta go hunt the cat. And it’s <i>sad</i> – it’ll stick in your throat. When the old man threw down his rifle and wept for shame I wept right along with him. Maybe not an ‘important’ work as far as the development of literature goes, but for spreading a message of conservation and respect </span>
  <span id="freeText8661736256472709781" style="display:none">Should be a bestseller. Could easily have been overpowered by sentimentality but it wasn’t. A kind of murder mystery where a big cat’s the killer and the mystery’s solved as soon as it’s introduced, but then they’ve gotta go hunt the cat. And it’s <i>sad</i> – it’ll stick in your throat. When the old man threw down his rifle and wept for shame I wept right along with him. Maybe not an ‘important’ work as far as the development of literature goes, but for spreading a message of conservation and respect for other species and tribes and customs without new age soppiness, it’s a winner. It helped that I read it in a rainforest – a temperate one as tame as a garden compared to this desolate corner of Ecuador, but enough to help set the scene. Oh, and it won’t depress you, just remind you of what’s right. An old-fashioned morality tale and easy to read. <br /></span>

<div id="review_1191436869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1191436869" />
    <a title="Book Concierge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1628041-book-concierge"><img alt="Book Concierge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324904606p2/1628041.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1191436869?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Book Concierge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Book Concierge" href="/user/show/1628041-book-concierge">Book Concierge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=philosophy">philosophy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=culture">culture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=latino-literature">latino-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=nature">nature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=concierge">concierge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=literature">literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1191436869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8834388935036930040"><u>From the book jacket</u>: An old man lives in a village on the Nangaritza River. The village is so small the dentist comes only twice a year, to pull teeth and bring books to the old man – love stories, the kind with maximum heartache. This is a story of the jungle, green hell and Eden; of the Shuar Indians, who know how to live in harmony with it; of the machines and settlers and gold prospectors and gringos who have invaded it. Nature, out of balance, becomes vengeful and violent. <br/><br/><u>My reactions</u>:<br/>Wha</span>
  <span id="freeText8834388935036930040" style="display:none"><u>From the book jacket</u>: An old man lives in a village on the Nangaritza River. The village is so small the dentist comes only twice a year, to pull teeth and bring books to the old man – love stories, the kind with maximum heartache. This is a story of the jungle, green hell and Eden; of the Shuar Indians, who know how to live in harmony with it; of the machines and settlers and gold prospectors and gringos who have invaded it. Nature, out of balance, becomes vengeful and violent. <br /><br /><u>My reactions</u>:<br />What a beautifully written story. I couldn’t help but think of my father – the way he knew the land and respected the animals who made it their home. There is a certain amount of philosophy expressed here – respect for nature, the foolishly aggressive humans making a mess out of paradise. The old man wants only to live in harmony with the jungle, not to conquer it. <br /><br />The writing is poetic and atmospheric, with a great sense of place. I felt the heat and humidity of the rainy season. Felt my skin crawl with insects. Heard the sounds of the jungle – the splash of a fish jumping out of the water, the whoosh of wings as a bird or bat took flight, the rustle of leaves made by a large animal moving through the undergrowth. Felt both the peace and terror of a pitch black night. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8834388935036930040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer347123570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8933530150295064460">This is how you make a book that is just an experience to read. Very easy to read, very short, very light on pretentions. Some may find it excesively simplistic: the good guys are good, the bad guys are bad; but I do not think this is a bad thing. I think there is a place for novels with clear-cut morals, in moderation, and done right. And this is a great example on how to do it right. Bolivar is just a great character and you are just left wishing a person like him really exists in this world. </span>
  <span id="freeText8933530150295064460" style="display:none">This is how you make a book that is just an experience to read. Very easy to read, very short, very light on pretentions. Some may find it excesively simplistic: the good guys are good, the bad guys are bad; but I do not think this is a bad thing. I think there is a place for novels with clear-cut morals, in moderation, and done right. And this is a great example on how to do it right. Bolivar is just a great character and you are just left wishing a person like him really exists in this world. Respectful to nature, capable, with a love for beauty and art...he's just a great hero. The nitpick data on life on the Amazon is also very interesting and even tough I guess the pro-nature message could be considered preachy it at least seems sincere and justified.<br />I loved it, plain and simple.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/433477842?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4705693-beth">Beth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4705693-beth?shelf=around-the-world-group">around-the-world-group</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4705693-beth?shelf=6-books-6-countries-6-continents">6-books-6-countries-6-continents</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer433477842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1123378080669603215"><i>Antonio José BolÍvar Proaño knew he could return to his village in the mountains. The poor forgive everything but failure.<br/><br/>He had no choice but to remain with only his memories for company. He wanted to take revenge on that accursed region, that green hell that had snatched away his beloved and his dreams. He pictured a huge blaze that would turn the entire Amazon into a raging fire.<br/><br/>Yet in his helplessness he discovered he didn't know the jungle well enough to hate it.<br/><br/>He learned the language of t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1123378080669603215" style="display:none"><i>Antonio José BolÍvar Proaño knew he could return to his village in the mountains. The poor forgive everything but failure.<br /><br />He had no choice but to remain with only his memories for company. He wanted to take revenge on that accursed region, that green hell that had snatched away his beloved and his dreams. He pictured a huge blaze that would turn the entire Amazon into a raging fire.<br /><br />Yet in his helplessness he discovered he didn't know the jungle well enough to hate it.<br /><br />He learned the language of the Shuar by joining their hunting expeditions. They hunted tapirs, pacas, capybaras, peccaries, small, very tasty wild boar, monkeys, birds, and reptiles. He learned to make good use of the blow pipe, which was so silent and effective in hunting, and of spears to catch the swift-moving fish.<br /><br />In their company, he abandoned his Catholic peasant prudishness. He went half-naked and avoided contact with the new settlers, who considered him a madman. <br /><br />Antonio José Bolívar Proaño, who never thought about the word "freedom" in the jungle, enjoyed limitless freedom. However much he tried to revive his old feeling of hatred, he couldn't help loving that world, and then the hatred faded as he was seduced by those vast expanses without frontier or owner.</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/762211.The_Old_Man_Who_Read_Love_Stories" title="The Old Man Who Read Love Stories by Luis Sepúlveda" rel="nofollow noopener">The Old Man Who Read Love Stories</a> is a short and beautiful little book. I think of it as an Ecuadorean <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2165.The_Old_Man_and_the_Sea" title="The Old Man and the Sea by Ernest Hemingway" rel="nofollow noopener">The Old Man and the Sea</a>. It is the story of a white man who for a time lives among the natives but can, in the end, not be one of them. He nonetheless carries their wisdom with him as he returns to the white settlements and never truly fits in among his own people. At the same time, his understanding of the jungle is respected. The villagers seek him out when their encounters with the wilderness become dangerous. The old man has errors to atone for, and is it in his encounters with the dangerous natural world that he seeks his redemption. Based on this novel, I would definitely be interested in reading more of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1084267.Luis_Sep_lveda" title="Luis Sepúlveda" rel="nofollow noopener">Luis Sepúlveda</a>’s work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1123378080669603215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25128624-nicole?shelf=dispo-bu-droit-lettres">dispo-bu-droit-lettres</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1759419029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7339417831687105241"><i>Il était reconnaissant à l'auteur de désigner les méchants dès le départ. De cette manière, on évitait les malentendus et les sympathies non méritées.</i><br/><br/>That sentences tells you quite a bit about what you need to know to read this little novel. <br/><br/>Personally, I'm not a fan of the formulaic romance and its clear villain. I'm certainly not, from the comfort of my centrally-heated, indoor plumbing, rapid internet connection, multiple libraries at my disposal, painkillers and antibiotics when I need them </span>
  <span id="freeText7339417831687105241" style="display:none"><i>Il était reconnaissant à l'auteur de désigner les méchants dès le départ. De cette manière, on évitait les malentendus et les sympathies non méritées.</i><br /><br />That sentences tells you quite a bit about what you need to know to read this little novel. <br /><br />Personally, I'm not a fan of the formulaic romance and its clear villain. I'm certainly not, from the comfort of my centrally-heated, indoor plumbing, rapid internet connection, multiple libraries at my disposal, painkillers and antibiotics when I need them intellectually stimulating life going to nod in agreement about how the "limace" is ridiculous because he wants to wear shoes in the jungle, or light a fire at night because he is afraid, or have something nice to eat. (The others mock him for wanting toilet paper, ffs.) I am fairly confident in saying that whenever my death comes, it won't be at the paws of a giant jungle cat, and I don't see why it's not okay to be grateful for that, or desire it for others. (Or maybe all the five-starrers think that those limits are fine for brown people who live in jungles, but not for westerners in the developed world who have a tenure file to assemble? Perhaps that's too harsh, but at a minimum there's a substantial amount of romanticizing going on.) <br /><br />Personally, I think a stronger book would not have created this particular villain, nor reveled quite so much in the mutilated corpses of the gold miners and american tourists. But then, I lack the simple wisdom that allows me to catch my own crabs barehanded for breakfast, believe ridiculous superstitions about how to kill a man so that his victim's ghost can rest, and then lose myself in stories of thwarted love. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89460656" />
    <a title="Irwan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/183639-irwan"><img alt="Irwan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442987463p2/183639.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89460656?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irwan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irwan" href="/user/show/183639-irwan">Irwan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/183639-irwan?shelf=finished">finished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/183639-irwan?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89460656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17674628666383209507">A charming and well composed short novel. It intimately describes the relationship of man and nature. The old man who reads love stories and the jungle of Amazon. His love of reading stories, despite the contrast with the savageness of his life and surroundings, does resonate to me. It shows how reading fulfils a certain, inevitable need of man even in the most unlikely situation. At times I felt this detail simply cosmetic to the story, but I don't mind that.<br/><br/>The real love story that moves me is</span>
  <span id="freeText17674628666383209507" style="display:none">A charming and well composed short novel. It intimately describes the relationship of man and nature. The old man who reads love stories and the jungle of Amazon. His love of reading stories, despite the contrast with the savageness of his life and surroundings, does resonate to me. It shows how reading fulfils a certain, inevitable need of man even in the most unlikely situation. At times I felt this detail simply cosmetic to the story, but I don't mind that.<br /><br />The real love story that moves me is the love of the female jaguar who takes revenge after her cubs killed and her mate wounded. It was a work of man. An intruder. The scene where she makes the old man kill the male jaguar to relieve him from the pain of slow death is one of my favourites. <br /><br />There is something poetic about that female jaguar and her revenge. The sheer energy of survival of the creatures of the jungle - including the old man - humbles me, a tamed creature of civilization who foolishly shares the delusion that we, humans, are actually the centre of the universe and have the rights to do anything we want of this earth. Shame on us!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17674628666383209507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_786457798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/786457798" />
    <a title="Mary Soderstrom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10505847-mary-soderstrom"><img alt="Mary Soderstrom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488296517p2/10505847.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/786457798?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Soderstrom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Soderstrom" href="/user/show/10505847-mary-soderstrom">Mary Soderstrom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer786457798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18351233049477728292">This was taken in Puerto Maldonado, on the Rio Madre de Deus in the Amazon basin. The bustling little city (population about 140,000) is where you used to have to take a ferry across the river to continue west into the Amazon.<br/><br/>But now a new bridge links the two sides, making it possible to go ride on reasonably good road from the Pacific coast of Peru, across Brazil and on to the Atlantic.<br/><br/>Travelling the highway was one of the reasons I went to South America a few weeks ago. A trip like that makes</span>
  <span id="freeText18351233049477728292" style="display:none">This was taken in Puerto Maldonado, on the Rio Madre de Deus in the Amazon basin. The bustling little city (population about 140,000) is where you used to have to take a ferry across the river to continue west into the Amazon.<br /><br />But now a new bridge links the two sides, making it possible to go ride on reasonably good road from the Pacific coast of Peru, across Brazil and on to the Atlantic.<br /><br />Travelling the highway was one of the reasons I went to South America a few weeks ago. A trip like that makes you think about many things, including new understanding of books you read a long time ago. <br /><br />One of these is Luis Supelveda's delightful The Old Man Who Read Love Stories. The thumbnail plot outline is: "In a remote river town deep in the Ecuadoran jungle, Antonio Jos Bolvar seeks refuge in amorous novels. But tourists and opportunists are making inroads into the area, and the balance of nature is making a dangerous shift."<br /><br />Well, yes, that's what I remember. But there's much more to it, including a character who is a teeth-pullling dentist and who removes all the teeth of a gold-hunter on a bet. The description is chillingly funny, but it turns out that there's an allegorical twist, since the Brazilian national hero who pioneered settlement of the hinterland is called Tiradentes, the tooth-puller. <br /><br />Sepulveda is a Chilean left wing activist in addition to being a playwright and novelist, and was a good friend of Chico Mendes, a Brazilian from a few miles east of Puerto Maldonado. Mendes was assasinated 25 years ago for leading a revolt of rubber tappers and protesting the rape of the Amazon. When you realize that, this charming little story--which can be read as tribute to the power of fiction to transport--becomes much more serious. It even can be read as the reverse of what it appears on the surface--that is, as a call to action, instead of an elegy for escape. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18351233049477728292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Sepulveda crafts an amazonian tale showcasing a man's deep understanding of the jungle and his uneasy coexistence with it.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer849953844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9707540928856433720"> A relatively quick read but packs a punch about the effects of exploration in South America and its material and emotional costs to the natural and human world. Much like Things Fall Apart, this novel takes on the politics of colonialism, the intrusion of Western values on indigenous/tribal ways of life, and the costs of misreading. The Old Man is a strong-minded, likeable character who attempts to navigate different worlds he belongs to. His insights about the natural world and non-human anima</span>
  <span id="freeText9707540928856433720" style="display:none"> A relatively quick read but packs a punch about the effects of exploration in South America and its material and emotional costs to the natural and human world. Much like Things Fall Apart, this novel takes on the politics of colonialism, the intrusion of Western values on indigenous/tribal ways of life, and the costs of misreading. The Old Man is a strong-minded, likeable character who attempts to navigate different worlds he belongs to. His insights about the natural world and non-human animals' intelligence are significant to this tall-tale about the demise of arrogant greedy men who attempt to dominate and defy nature and the power of imaginative writing to heal and soothe trauma. And let's not forget the cat! She is a frightening and powerful figure, acting as a protector of the jungle and traditional ways of life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9707540928856433720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2645994706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10150333409233356318">I finished this in one sitting with a pot of tea, it’s a simple but beautifully written story about an old man in the jungle. He’s very likeable and there’s an interesting environmental slant to the story. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13211216098984813865">This is my first 5 star read in 2020. It is one of the last books I needed to complete my “equator-challenge”, to read a book from every country on the equator, this time Equador. I agree with 28% of the raters who also gave the novella 5 stars.<br/><br/>I read literature to travel to unknown places. To experience them through the eyes and words of authors.   <span id="freeText13211216098984813865" style="display:none">This is my first 5 star read in 2020. It is one of the last books I needed to complete my “equator-challenge”, to read a book from every country on the equator, this time Equador. I agree with 28% of the raters who also gave the novella 5 stars.<br /><br />I read literature to travel to unknown places. To experience them through the eyes and words of authors. This book gave me an exceptional experience. The hero, who is as described, an old man who reads love stories, is a unique, multidimensional character. I loved everything about him. Amazonia was brought to life (and death) through Sepulveda’s descriptive writing. It wasn’t glamorized, but real and harsh and alive. The other people in the book, some rather stereotyped caricatures, still resonate with personality and are made vivid by the unique, sometimes sarcastic, descriptive language of the author. <br /><br />A strong recommendation.<br /><br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3359968851" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3359968851" />
    <a title="Cristi Ivan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/93976803-cristi-ivan"><img alt="Cristi Ivan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583394342p2/93976803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3359968851?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristi Ivan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristi Ivan" href="/user/show/93976803-cristi-ivan">Cristi Ivan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3359968851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14242694624178635221"><b> The Old Man Who Read Love Stories</b> by Luis Sepulveda is an astonishing tale of solitude of a man who only dreams of love. At the same time, it’s an ode to nature and the way we should live our life in perfect harmony with it. <br/><br/>Antonio Jose Bolivar is an old man who lives alone in a small Ecuadorian village, right at the edge of the Amazonian jungle, on the bank of Nangaritza river. He came from the mountains, long ago, together with his wife, Dolores Encarnacion del Santisimo Sacramento Estupinan</span>
  <span id="freeText14242694624178635221" style="display:none"><b> The Old Man Who Read Love Stories</b> by Luis Sepulveda is an astonishing tale of solitude of a man who only dreams of love. At the same time, it’s an ode to nature and the way we should live our life in perfect harmony with it. <br /><br />Antonio Jose Bolivar is an old man who lives alone in a small Ecuadorian village, right at the edge of the Amazonian jungle, on the bank of Nangaritza river. He came from the mountains, long ago, together with his wife, Dolores Encarnacion del Santisimo Sacramento Estupinan Otavalo. <br /><br />All the way through the book, the author always uses Dolores’ full name and although it gave the novel a slightly comic note, its initials are a little bit too close to the Spanish word <b>deseo</b>. And this book is about yearning, the desire to find true, passionate love, to bring back the natural balance of the environment, that has long been tainted by the Western civilization.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[After the death of his wife,  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>Antonio Jose Bolivar starts to spend more and more time with the indigenous population of Shuars, learning to live in good harmony with the nature. Now old, his only joy in life is the arrival of the dentist, twice a year, who brings him two books each time, recommended by a prostitute.<br /><br />Antonio Jose Bolivar's desire for love is reflected in the heartbreaking story of the female jaguar, whose cubs and pairs are killed by a gold prospector. The female jaguar and Antonio’s fate intertwine throughout the novel, reaching a tragic conclusion.<br /><br />The writing style is marvelous. While reading this novel, I felt a constant coldness and humidity. On the background of my thoughts, I heard the constant sound of rain falling on the leaves of the Ecuadorian rainforest. It was beautiful and I really recommend this novel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14242694624178635221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3359968851">

<div id="review_3365027981" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3365027981" />
    <a title="Catalin Constantin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36552165-catalin-constantin"><img alt="Catalin Constantin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457962047p2/36552165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3365027981?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catalin Constantin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catalin Constantin" href="/user/show/36552165-catalin-constantin">Catalin Constantin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3365027981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer83999585905936060">A simple moralizing tale about nature and the overincreasing involvement of humans in it.<br/><br/>The story focuses on Antonio Bolivar, an old Ecuadorian man living on the edge of civilization and of the Amazonian jungle, living the remainder of his life in a simple manner, respecting and benefiniting from the surrounding nature, and finding comfort in love novels brought to him by the dentist who visits the remote village two times a year.<br/><br/>We learn about the past life of the man, his short marriage and h</span>
  <span id="freeText83999585905936060" style="display:none">A simple moralizing tale about nature and the overincreasing involvement of humans in it.<br /><br />The story focuses on Antonio Bolivar, an old Ecuadorian man living on the edge of civilization and of the Amazonian jungle, living the remainder of his life in a simple manner, respecting and benefiniting from the surrounding nature, and finding comfort in love novels brought to him by the dentist who visits the remote village two times a year.<br /><br />We learn about the past life of the man, his short marriage and his life with the local Shuar tribe until the arrival of the Westerners has overturned everything and he was forced to leave the jungle for the village born nearby from colonizers and people searching for their fortune elsewhere. <br /><br />As the story progresses, the predominant quiet life of the old man is disturbed by violent clashes between man and nature, and he is forced to intervene.<br /><br />Antonio's tale somewhat reminded me of another famous short novel, Hemingway's The old man and the sea, another story that meditates upon the condition of man and his struggles with nature and its elements.<br /><br />4 stars from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="83999585905936060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3210225084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3210225084" />
    <a title="Leni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44811987-leni"><img alt="Leni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597748877p2/44811987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3210225084?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leni" href="/user/show/44811987-leni">Leni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789607073150" href="/book/show/12263497">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3210225084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6003233123258453054">This must be one of the most moving and captivating books I've ever read. The description of the exotic Amazon sceneries are exquisite. My favourite thing, though, is that the author portrays civilised humans as idiotic barbarians spoiling the untouched natural habitat of several magnificent species of animals and you can't help but sympathize with the animals after the monstrosities mentioned. Once I get to a couple more of his works I'm sure Sepulveda will have already gained a place among my </span>
  <span id="freeText6003233123258453054" style="display:none">This must be one of the most moving and captivating books I've ever read. The description of the exotic Amazon sceneries are exquisite. My favourite thing, though, is that the author portrays civilised humans as idiotic barbarians spoiling the untouched natural habitat of several magnificent species of animals and you can't help but sympathize with the animals after the monstrosities mentioned. Once I get to a couple more of his works I'm sure Sepulveda will have already gained a place among my favourites!</span>

<div id="review_2043244085" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2043244085" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/687370-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296162711p2/687370.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2043244085?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/687370-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2043244085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6940567421180691195">Aside from having one of the best titles ever, this novella is quite captivating and painted a vivid picture of life in the Amazon jungle. A little too vivid for this wary traveler hoping to avoid snake bites and big jungle cats. I loved how the man relished the first words of the romance novel "Paul kissed her ardently" and the author made me truly feel his wanderlust.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3313798825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3313798825" />
    <a title="Gerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11108005-gerry"><img alt="Gerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342739769p2/11108005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3313798825?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gerry" href="/user/show/11108005-gerry">Gerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780151685509" href="/book/show/1184633.The_Old_Man_Who_Read_Love_Stories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11108005-gerry?shelf=around-the-world">around-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11108005-gerry?shelf=translated">translated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3313798825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1853776985406572551">I would love to read more by Sepúlveda, who died in April 2020 from COVID-19. That his first novel, about an old man in the Amazonian jungle, could so enthrall me, seems to bode very well for the quality of his subsequent works. His writing is spare but evocative, bringing the setting and his characters clearly to life without a single wasted word. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g+gMvkmbp0yYjO3M8O4JM7XYCM7vqCWEwl10VKLrsmonSTPfDtPBrrkymnyDvnZsWksNfc99XqQG9G9kniuSOg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Je1YSrQwd7jbD5hOkK0JYerkGIMgQ17uXfUmHaWdeueBTGcr83gRWvqx7/7j/XY+BXcdMACWJc6ZXD0tmV1atw==')})
  }

E che cosa contengono queste pillole? Per rispondere alla prima domanda, basta guardarsi attorno. Viviamo in una società “a gradini” che ancora oggi offre opportunità diverse a soggetti con caratteristiche differenti: non solo a uomini e donne, ma anche a bianchi e neri, persone etero- e omosessuali e via dicendo. Siamo talmente abituati a vederci attorniati da queste situazioni di privilegio e discriminazione che talvolta non le riconosciamo neppure come tali o le consideriamo “normali”. ma siamo sicuri che, a prescindere dalla nostra personale condizione di privilegio, possiamo vivere sereni in un mondo in cui una donna, a pari mansioni e competenze, guadagna meno di un uomo, o dove chi non risponde a canoni estetici più o meno espliciti si vergogna e magari non trova nemmeno lavoro, o dove un uomo non può permettersi di essere emotivo? Ecco, quindi, il senso di questo libro: offrire uno strumento per costruire rapporti paritari e porre le basi per una società davvero inclusiva, dove tutti, anche coloro che stanno in posizioni di potere, possano trarne beneficio e vivere meglio. A questo scopo – passiamo ora al contenuto delle pillole –, l’autrice Irene facheris esamina una a una le discriminazioni più diffuse (dalla rape culture al sessismo benevolo, dalla omobitransfobia al Classicismo) per invitare tutte e tutti a diffondere attivamente una sensibilità nuova. Perché – come spiega facheris – “Il personale è politico” ovvero, se il mio problema è diffuso, non è più solo mio e insieme possiamo affrontarlo più efficacemente. Quando un oggetto di valore si rompe, in Giappone, lo si ripara con oro liquido. È un’antica tecnica che mostra e non nasconde le fratture. Le esibisce come un pregio: cicatrici dorate, segno orgoglioso di rinascita. Anche per le persone è così. Chi ha sofferto è prezioso, la fragilità può trasformarsi in forza. La tecnica che salda i pezzi, negli uomini, si chiama amore. Questa è la storia di Irina, che ha combattuto una battaglia e l’ha vinta. Una donna che non dimentica il passato, al contrario: lo ricorda, lo porta al petto come un fiore.Irina ha una vita serena, ordinata. Un marito, due figlie gemelle. È italiana, vive in Svizzera, lavora come avvocato. Un giorno qualcosa si incrina. Il matrimonio finisce, senza traumi apparenti. In un fine settimana qualsiasi Mathias, il padre delle bambine, porta via Alessia e Livia. Spariscono. Qualche giorno dopo l’uomo si uccide. Delle bambine non c’è più nessuna traccia.Pagina dopo pagina, rivelazione dopo rivelazione, in un ritmo che fa di questo libro un autentico thriller psicologico e insieme un superbo ritratto di donna, coraggiosa e fragile, Irina conquista brandelli sempre più luminosi di verità e ricuce la sua vita. Da quel fondo oscuro, doloroso, arriva una luce nuova. La possibilità di amare ancora, l’amore che salda e che resta.Concita De Gregorio prende i fatti, semplici e terribili, ed entra nella voce della protagonista. Indagando a fondo una storia vera crea un congegno narrativo rapido, incalzante e pieno di sorprese. Disegna un ritratto memorabile di donna del nostro tempo. Scandisce l’esistenza di questa madre privata dei figli – qual è la parola per dirlo? – in lettere, messaggi, elenchi. Irina scrive alla nonna, al fratello, al giudice, alla maestra delle gemelle, abbozza ritratti, scava nei gesti, torna alle sue radici, trova infine un approdo. Dimenticare significa portare fuori dalla mente, ricordare è tenere nel cuore. Il bisogno di essere ancora felice, ripetuto a voce alta, una sfida contro le frasi fatte, contro i giudizi e i pregiudizi. Uno di quei libri in cui uomini e donne trovano qualcosa di sé.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"13195736798734282512\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n
